<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence вҖ” no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- sensei: teacher, instructor
- kyoutou: deputy head teacher, vice principal
- kateikyoushi: home tutor, private tutor
- omoi: heavy, weighty
- kurasumeito: classmate

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- гӮҲгҒҸгҒӘгҒЈгҒҹ (yokunaru): to become better [Past tense]
- гҒҠгӮӮгҒ„гҒҫгҒҷ (omou): to think [Polite/Formal form]
- гӮҸгӮӢгҒҸгҒҰ (warui): bad [Te-form]
- гҒҹгҒ№гӮүгӮҢгҒӘгҒӢгҒЈгҒҹ (taberu): to eat [Potential / Passive, Negative, Past tense]

TONE HINT:
- taichou: physical condition

Input: sensei komichi taicho yokunatta genki aru to de mo omoimasu memai ga kibun warukute taberarenakatta
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence вҖ” no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- miru: to see, to look
- dekiru: to be able to do, to be possible
- miru: to go around
- jitsuyou: practical use, utility
- kotogadekiru: to be able to, to be possible to

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- гӮҲгӮ“гҒ гӮҠ (yobu): to call out to [Such things as (tari)]
- гҒ“гҒЁ: (you) should (grammar pattern)
- гҒ§гҒҚгҒҫгҒӣгӮ“ (dekiru): to be able to do [Polite negative]

TONE HINT:
- deshouka: don't you think?

Input: shunbun wo yondari miru гҒ“гҒЁ shuuchuu dekimasen ka
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

<details>
<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence вҖ” no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- kudasai: please give me, please do for me
- takushii: taxi
- shuuzu: shoes
- pikkuappusaabisu: pickup service
- shatorubasu: shuttle bus

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:

<details>
<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence вҖ” no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- sensei: teacher, instructor
- saisho: beginning, outset
- sensei: head start, initiative
- korera: cholera
- jugyou: lesson, class

GRAMMAR & TENSE HINTS:
- гӮҸгҒӢгҒЈгҒҹ (wakaru): to understand [Past tense]
- гҒ„гҒҳгӮҮгҒҶ: so long as (grammar pattern)
- гӮҸгӮӢkгҒӘгҒ„ (warui): bad [Negative]

TONE HINT:
- hizuke: date

Input: wakatta sensei kore гҒ„гҒҳгӮҮгҒҶ warukunai ranai to iinokosu desu ga sugi no youyaku itsu desuka saisho chichi no hi de happyoukai aru no de
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

#### LLM Output
